  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_dd96fd3e-6688-4c05-94e9-4808256c428f'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer11477078039971514658">Katarina Bishop and W.W.   <span id="freeText11477078039971514658" style="display:none">Katarina Bishop and W.W. Hale the fifth were born to lead completely different lives: Kat comes from a long, proud line of loveable criminal masterminds, while Hale is the son of one of the most seemingly perfect dynasties in the world. If their families have one thing in common, it's that they both know how to stay under the radar while getting-or stealing-whatever they want. No matter the risk, the Bishops can always be counted on, but in Hale's family, all bets are off when money is on the line. When Hale unexpectedly inherits his grandmother's billion dollar corporation, he quickly learns that there's no place for Kat and their old heists in his new role. But Kat won't let him go that easily, especially after she gets tipped off that his grandmother's will might have been altered in an elaborate con to steal the company's fortune. Forced to keep a level head as she and her crew fight for one of their own, Kat comes up with an ambitious and far-reaching plan that only the Bishop family would dare attempt. To pull it off, Kat is prepared to do the impossible, but first, she has to decide if she's willing to save her boyfriend's company if it means losing the boy.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13936048219297321240">June 16th, 12. Pre-reading the book:<br/><br/><br/><b>OMGGGGGGGGGGGGGG IT'S HALE!</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380375765i/730411.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>IT'S A GIFT FROM GOD! <333333333333</b><br/><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380382002ra/739472.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/>February 9th, 13. AFTER reading the book:<br/><br/>I love the Heist Society series. I love that they're a thrill ride, I love its complexity and simplicity. It can do no wrong in my eyes.<br/><br/>However, much to my surprise (and dismay) Perfect Scoundrels ended up being my least favorite of the three. I can't really point out why, maybe because there wasn't a big heist in it or maybe because it was just so sad all th</span>
  <span id="freeText13936048219297321240" style="display:none">June 16th, 12. Pre-reading the book:<br><br><br><b>OMGGGGGGGGGGGGGG IT'S HALE!</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380375765i/730411.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>IT'S A GIFT FROM GOD! &lt;333333333333</b><br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380382002ra/739472.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>February 9th, 13. AFTER reading the book:<br><br>I love the Heist Society series. I love that they're a thrill ride, I love its complexity and simplicity. It can do no wrong in my eyes.<br><br>However, much to my surprise (and dismay) Perfect Scoundrels ended up being my least favorite of the three. I can't really point out why, maybe because there wasn't a big heist in it or maybe because it was just so sad all the time. <br><br>But don't get me wrong, I still think it was excellent. I still gave it five stars because it truly deserved them. I adored that Ally decided to dedicated some time to explore Hale as a bigger character and not just a love interest. I adore Hale, he is one of my ultimate boyfriends, but to be honest, we didn't have much information about him from the previous books, except for the fact that he's insanely rich and ultra loyal. I loved that we learned what we've been guessing all along: that his life isn't as perfect as you'd imagine, that his family is one of those you wouldn't want to have, and that his parents are snobs. There was a new vulnerability to Hale that Ally Carter had only let us glimpse in the past. So I absolutely loved that.<br><br>And Kat acting all worried over Hale was the icing on the cake. I mean I hate when girls made everything about themselves and start stealing the spotlight. Kat was Kat. The perfect, poised and mature girlfriend that just wanted to help her boyfriend, even if said boyfriend kept pushing her away. It was also so cool that all her family teamed up to help Hale. It showed that unity and love don't need blood bonds.<br><br>Overall, I think it was a great continuation to the story, but I am nowhere need done with this characters, I need more. And it sucks that we don’t even have a confirmation for a next book ):<br><br>PS. If you're a fan of Ally's work or if you've never picked up either of her series but would want to check if they'd be for you, then go and read her short story: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16301336.Double_Crossed_A_Spies_and_Thieves_Story__Gallagher_Girls___5_5__Heist_Society___2_5_" title="Double Crossed A Spies and Thieves Story (Gallagher Girls, #5.5; Heist Society, #2.5) by Ally Carter" rel="nofollow noopener">Double Crossed: A Spies and Thieves Story</a> it's a fun and entertaining cross over of both her series (and it includes Hale!).<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="13936048219297321240" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  <span id="freeText14917936903555730171" style="display:none">4.5 stars.<br><br>PRE-ORDERED!!!!<br><br>Hale. <b>HALE.</b> <i>ON THE COVER.</i><br> <br>There are no words to express what this book will do to me. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/652659.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/390109.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/390110.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>ONE MORE MONTH. 4 MORE WEEKS. 30 SOME ODD DAYS. <br><br>....<br>At 10:06, a truck pulled up to my house.<br>At 10:08, the doorbell rang.<br>At 10:08.26, the neighbors heard some screeching and wondered where it was coming from.<br>At 11:36, My sister and I grabbed our books and headed to the couch.<br>At 11:37, we smiled, high fived, and gleefully read the opening scene that we'd be asking for for years.<br>At 3:48, I read the last sentence of page 118, closed my book , and proceeded to go into hysterics.<br>At 4:53, I got to a scene in which my babies were semi-happy again and thus, I was happy.<br>At 5:16, I realized just how appropriate it was that Ally wanted to name this book "The Big Book of Brooding Shirtless Hale." (Too bad it got vetoed by the publisher...)<br><br>...<br><br>So you know that scene? That scene that every single reader asked for and Ally was super evasive about? The one that she said she'd probably never do? Well, it's in here. And it's pretty much everything I hoped for.<br><br>...<br><br>So very good. <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/465906.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>*deep breath* <br><br>The con was so/so at the beginning, but then again, they always are. And then you get to the end and you have to just nod in approval.<br><br>...<br><br>All the <s>Hale brooding</s> relationship angst got a little old but strangely wasn't that annoying. And I did feel sorry for him, the poor dear. His family is...awful. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The only one who cared for him and that he cared for was Hazel and with her gone and all the weight of his family's pressures and the fact that he owns the company ad he doesn't want Kat involved in it because he knows that that's not her life and then he's trying to deal with the fact that with all his new responsibility in Hale Industries, he won't be able to hang out with the Bishops and their crew as much and....he's just broody. Plus, he gets upset, understandably so, when Kat starts running the con without him, without even a by-your-leave. I don't excuse him completely for being mean to Kat but he's off the hook a bit.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>And then Kat is dealing with Hale being broody... It's a mess. A good mess, but a mess.<br>...<br><br>Kat's family is the bomb. Seriously, they are the BEST. I <u>adored</u> getting more of them in the book. Bobby, Uncle Eddie, Uncle Roy, Aunt Irina, Uncle Felix, and a bunch of uncles I can no longer remember. I loved all the scenes with all the uncles crowded in Uncle Eddie's kitchen. I live for family relationships like that...<br>...<br><br>I loved it. Cannot even say how much I would lOVE another one. Or three. Or ten.<br><br><br>Fan-Mix:<br><br>1. <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=xYN3GZ0316Y" rel="nofollow noopener">Everybody Lies</a> (Jason Walker) - Hale<br><br>2. <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=riVjjr3ekiE" rel="nofollow noopener">Feel</a> (Marie Digby) - Kat<br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

  <span id="freeText16445546863485525120" style="display:none">Sabrina was innocently surfing the Internet when she read there was going to be a 3rd installment to the Heist Society. Eager, Sabrina went on to Goodreads hoping to be given some information on what the book will be about. This was what she recieved:<br><br><img src="https://www.goodreads.com/assets/nocover-blank-133x176.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>....<br><br>....<br><br>....<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/482015.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Sabrina is not pleased. Curious, Sabrina clicked her pre-review to be met with ... A COVER!<br><br>The cover:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1340716595l/13580928.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Initial reaction:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380375765ra/730409.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Followed by ...<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380375765ra/730410.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Suffice to say, I cannot wait! And seeing this cover only makes me <s>want</s> need this book even more!<br><br><u>Digging a <i>little</i> deeper</u><br>There are some certain things we can get out of this cover like the fact that there's Hale in the sunglasses reflection. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380375765i/730411.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Or who I am assuming is Hale, I'd feel pretty damn embarassed if it turns out to be Nick or Simon.<br><br>Either way, cute guy in the sunglasses reflection!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/519760.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The fact that Kat is wearing pink just makes me feel giddy inside ... probably just me. <br><br>And then in their eye, we see a reflection of what looks to be typical NYC taxis. Yeah, I'm overanalysing this!<br><br>Anyways, I am <i>so</i> happy we have more information (like, since did Kat and Hale become a couple?)! Until next time, Sabrina signing out!</span>

<div id="review_524150342" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/524150342" />
    <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library"><img alt="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350750103p2/4551536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/524150342?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library">Maja (The Nocturnal Library)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781408326459" href="/book/show/15848609-perfect-scoundrels">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=just-another-book-crush">just-another-book-crush</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=own-a-dtb">own-a-dtb</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=reviewed-in-2013">reviewed-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=arc-2013">arc-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=hachette">hachette</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=all-the-right-choices">all-the-right-choices</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=best-of-2013">best-of-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=role-models">role-models</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=contemporary-fiction">contemporary-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer524150342" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2193283321520593162"><b>4.5 stars</b><br/>Perfect Scoundrels was my Waiting on Wednesday pick just over a month ago, and no wonder; I’ve been looking forward to it for months. I loved Heist Society and I loved Uncommon Criminals (although maybe just a tiny bit less), but Perfect Scoundrels exceeded all my expectations. It was by far the best of the series, exciting and virtually unputdownable. <br/>Finally (finally!) things moved forward between Kat and Hale, but just as Kat recovered from the panic attack their new girlfriend-boyfr</span>
  <span id="freeText2193283321520593162" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b><br>Perfect Scoundrels was my Waiting on Wednesday pick just over a month ago, and no wonder; I’ve been looking forward to it for months. I loved Heist Society and I loved Uncommon Criminals (although maybe just a tiny bit less), but Perfect Scoundrels exceeded all my expectations. It was by far the best of the series, exciting and virtually unputdownable. <br>Finally (finally!) things moved forward between Kat and Hale, but just as Kat recovered from the panic attack their new girlfriend-boyfriend status caused her, the news came that Hale’s grandmother is dead and that he inherited his family’s billion dollar company. <br><br>In Perfect Scoundrels, Kat and her crew face the most cunning enemy yet, and the stakes are even higher because they’re defending one of their own. W.W. Hale the Fifth may be an heir and a billionaire, but he is also the most loyal, wonderful person any of them has ever met. Kat’s entire family (and it’s a <i>very</i> large family) will have to work together to fix the mess and steal back the boy that has become irreplaceable to them all. As difficult as that sounds, it’s still easier said than done. Kat’s usual crew – Gabrielle, Nick, Simon and the Bagshaw brothers – will need help from their elders if they’re to outsmart Hale’s enemies and save his company. <br><br><b>
  <i>It was exactly what Kat would have done – what she had done on a number of occasions – and she felt the sting that comes from knowing that turnabout is absolutely not fair play.</i>
</b><br><br>In this emotionally difficult situation, Kat shined brighter than ever. I’ve always admired her, but here she showed the presence of mind and astounding maturity one simply doesn’t expect from a 16-year-old, not even an accomplished thief. Hale always seemed more mature to me, but that was not the case in Perfect Scoundrels. While he was busy mourning and showing us his more vulnerable side, Kat was fighting everyone (including him at times) to steal back the boy she just wasn’t ready to let go.<br><br>Once again, Ally Carter’s trademark sense of humor shone from every page, but in this book, she showed a different side of her characters as well – a frightened, more vulnerable side that gave them more credibility. I’ve complained in my earlier reviews that this series lacks emotional depth, but that’s not the case anymore. Finally these characters are three-dimensional. I just hope this won’t be the last time we get to see it.<br><br>I think my overall enjoyment of this series is largely due to my love for W.W. Hale the Fifth. He is the perfect love interest (and possibly a hero in his own right) , good looking and genuinely nice, but mysterious enough to keep me on my toes the entire time. He still didn’t share what W.W. stands for, although he came very close in one heartbreaking scene, but we did get to learn the nickname his family uses for him, and let me tell you, it’s not one you’re likely to forget. *g*<br><br>Objectively speaking, this isn’t a 4.5-star book, but I gave it the extra half just because it made me happy – and objectivity be damned. It’s my party after all, and I fervently wish there were more books like Perfect Scoundrels out there. I’d read them all. And then I’d re-read them.<br><br><a href="http://www.thenocturnallibrary.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380226536i/681142.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>

    <a title="Amelia, free market Puritan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan"><img alt="Amelia, free market Puritan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508223427p2/1852293.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

I read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10327303.Uncommon_Criminals__Heist_Society___2_' title='Uncommon Criminals (Heist Society, #2) by Ally Carter' rel='nofollow noopener'>Uncommon Criminals</a> almost a year ago, so I'm shoddy on the details.   <span id="freeText5382167093327236857" style="display:none">Wait, wait, hold the phone. I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10327303.Uncommon_Criminals__Heist_Society___2_" title="Uncommon Criminals (Heist Society, #2) by Ally Carter" rel="nofollow noopener">Uncommon Criminals</a> almost a year ago, so I'm shoddy on the details. <div id="review_527211949" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/527211949" />
    <a title="Mitch" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8170554-mitch"><img alt="Mitch" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1396208595p2/8170554.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/527211949?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mitch" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mitch" href="/user/show/8170554-mitch">Mitch</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer527211949" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer236095449616232294">Dear Ally Carter super fan who used the old 'I need it for my summer reading assignment' excuse to buy the hardcover of <i>Uncommon Criminals</i> and then actually did your book report on <i>Uncommon Criminals</i> (you know who you are):<br/><br/>There are two ways I could do this review. I could claim I've always been an Ally Carter fan and proceed straight to the animated gif spam, but that would be a lie. Plus, as you know, that's not really my style; I'm far more comfortable expressing myself with the written word </span>
  <span id="freeText236095449616232294" style="display:none">Dear Ally Carter super fan who used the old 'I need it for my summer reading assignment' excuse to buy the hardcover of <i>Uncommon Criminals</i> and then actually did your book report on <i>Uncommon Criminals</i> (you know who you are):<br /><br />There are two ways I could do this review. I could claim I've always been an Ally Carter fan and proceed straight to the animated gif spam, but that would be a lie. Plus, as you know, that's not really my style; I'm far more comfortable expressing myself with the written word than a bunch of snarky images. Or, I could give you a bunch of pithy, crowd pleasing quotes like '<i>Perfect Scoundrels</i> is the best Ally Carter <b>
  <i>ever</i>
</b>!' or 'Ally Carter has distilled rappelling off tall buildings, breaking and entering the world's most secure locations, and looking good while doing it into an art form!' and that at least would be truthful. So even if I don't share your overall enthusiasm for Ally Carter's books and will continue to insist the first two <i>Heist Societies</i> weren't that good, please get off my case because I'll man up and admit <i>Perfect Scoundrels</i> is a pretty good book. Just stop bothering me until after the next <i>Gallagher Girls</i> comes out. I mean it.<br /><br />Ok, so you want to hear me sing the praises of this book some more before you'll leave me alone? Fine. Just don't be mad with some of my points. Like, you know what the first two books were missing? Character. Yeah, I know Katarina Bishop is a cat burglar, and kind of an awesome one at that, and she gets two love interests, one the supposedly amazing billionaire Hale who just follows her around helping her steal stuff, and the other Nick, who's kind of lame, but I'm just tired of you going on about 'Hale this' and 'Hale that' that I decided to root for Nick, first out of spite, but then because I ended up genuinely liking the character because he at least wasn’t a total Marty Stu, and then of course Ally Carter had to Josh him, but that’s neither here nor there. Because even if you may insist otherwise, I swear the real reason the first two books fell flat for me is because even though Kat is cute and her antics amusing the whole Kat and Hale angle went over my head (read: bored the crap out of me) and the actual plot wasn’t that good no matter how ‘incredible’ (read: cutesy) Carter made breaking into a highly secure museum sound. And there were too many darn time jumps that made following the whole heist kinda hard! And the second one with the Cleopatra Emerald was even worse! Ahem. My apologies.<br /><br />Anyway, so yeah, I’ll admit I was skeptical about a Hale centric book, but, ok, sure, it totally works. (No, don’t jump up and down while I’m saying that. And gimme that pillow dammit!) Why? <i>Perfect Scoundrels</i> is a much better book because Carter does something I didn’t think she’d do. Character development! That makes Hale, yes, interesting! I’ve always wondered why a billionaire would help a cat burglar rob people, throwing in free flights on his private jet no less, but the Prologue answers that, and is kinda beautifully written to boot. Yeah, Carter’s writing is always something (read: I can see why you enjoy her books even if I’m less than impressed by the plots), but most of the time it leans more towards cute spy stuff than substantive, this book and the ending of <i>I’d Tell You I Love You But Then I’d Have to Kill You</i> / beginning of <i>Cross My Heart and Hope to Spy</i> aside. But yes, I liked the reveals about Hale’s past, how the heist this time really worked for Hale’s character development, how Kat and Hale’s relationship progressed as a result, and even how Kat’s family comes together to pull it off in the end that really shows Hale becoming part of her family, her world, as well.<br /><br />Of course, it helps too that this was the most interesting heist so far. Maybe it’s because it’s Hale’s company on the line this time, or maybe it’s because this plot is way different than the formula that’s been followed for the last two books now, but I liked it. Instead of the identifying the target, planning the heist, culminating in the actual crime plot as usual, this time there are actually twists and turns throughout, a couple of different objectives at different stages of the book, and a plot that’s not driven nearly by the single minded linearness that made <i>Uncommon Criminals</i> such a dull experience (read: disguising the motives of the villain doesn’t work if I predict it, I really need more to chew on than just that). Am I impressed that Nick gets Joshed again or that a couple of things like what happens to Uncle Eddie, the identity of Ms. Montenegro, or Natalie’s role in the whole thing are still really obvious? No, but I’ll let them slide for <b>
  <i>Scooter</i>
</b>. Let's dispense with the odd time jumps though.<br /><br />So, yeah, liked the book. Hope you’re happy.<br /><br />Sincerely,<br /><br />The guy who’s now out twelve bucks and change after buying this<br /><br />P.S. Did you like that fake out when you almost learned what the W stood for? :p</span>
  <a data-text-id="236095449616232294" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1064354496" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1064354496" />
    <a title="Sara (Freadom Library)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24190242-sara-freadom-library"><img alt="Sara (Freadom Library)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590346455p2/24190242.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1064354496?book_show_action=true">Sep 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara (Freadom Library)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara (Freadom Library)" href="/user/show/24190242-sara-freadom-library">Sara (Freadom Library)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17383871-perfect-scoundrels">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24190242-sara-freadom-library?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24190242-sara-freadom-library?shelf=finished-series">finished-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24190242-sara-freadom-library?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24190242-sara-freadom-library?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24190242-sara-freadom-library?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1064354496" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12331505407921696641">This was so good! But like, who the hell is Visily Romani??<br/><br/>This review was originally posted at <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://freadomlibrary.wordpress.com/'>https://freadomlibrary.wordpress.com/</a><br/><br/><b>Critically</b><br/>Plot – 5 out of 5 stars<br/>This is one of my favorite finales of all time. It was entertaining, action packed and intense. There were so many twists and turns that kept me on the edge of my seat. It had the romance that I wanted, the friendships that I wanted, the family relationships that I wanted but most of all, it was emotional and it showed a side of the</span>
  <span id="freeText12331505407921696641" style="display:none">This was so good! But like, who the hell is Visily Romani??<br /><br />This review was originally posted at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://freadomlibrary.wordpress.com/">https://freadomlibrary.wordpress.com/</a><br /><br /><b>Critically</b><br />Plot – 5 out of 5 stars<br />This is one of my favorite finales of all time. It was entertaining, action packed and intense. There were so many twists and turns that kept me on the edge of my seat. It had the romance that I wanted, the friendships that I wanted, the family relationships that I wanted but most of all, it was emotional and it showed a side of the characters that I wasn’t expecting but that I loved all the same.<br /><br />Writing Style – 4 out of 5 stars<br />I am a fan of Ally’s writing style since it’s simple, really easy to read and still manages to keep you guessing as the story goes on. There’s a kind of weaving storyline with lots of different point of views that have limited perspectives to the story and help keep the reader engaged. It’s funny, detailed and descriptive and helps fly through the books.<br /><br />Characters – 4 out of 5 stars<br />These characters managed to worm their way into my heart little by little though I still love the Gallagher Girls more. We get to see a more emotional side of Kat in this book. She’s usually very together and centered, at least on the outside. But the plot of this book and the things that are affecting Hale really scare her and she feels vulnerable when dealing with his emotions and change in attitude. However, she’s determined to help him. She’s sweet but cocky and smart at the same time and she got the job done. Hale had me almost weeping in this book. Poor guy has a really tough family life and this book showed us that side of him more. He’s angry, lost and sad. He’s vulnerable and hurt and starts to push away the people that love him because of that. Yet he’s determined to get to the bottom of what’s going on with the business his famly owns. One of my favorite parts of this book is the fact that Kat’s family all come together. I’ve always wanted to know more about them and it was awesome to finally have that happen. I loved it!<br /><br /><b>Emotionally</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[This is one of the best series endings I’ve ever read. It had everything that I’d been waiting for from this series.<br /><br />The plot is emotional. Things seem to be back to relatively normal for Kat when Hale’s grandmother dies and leaves him the family million dollar business. But Kat has a feeling that things aren’t right and after being approached by some people who believe the same, she starts to investigate. These books generally have a specific con or heist to pull off that spans the entire book and I really enjoyed that this one was a lot more personal, they are working to uncover a plot to help their friend instead of just another regular job. The differences between the types of jobs is clear and obvious, a lot more of family came in to help and everyone was a lot more emotionally invested. It also made me care more about the characters and it gave a deeper look into their relationships with each other. It had the common fast paced action with the lighthearted funny moments that make this series great, but with that more intense and caring edge that made this book so much more impactful when reading. It was nice to finally meet more of Kat’s family. We’ve been hearing about this huge group for awhile, even some of the main players and they finally showed up on page! This series has the ability to get me on my toes with so many of the twists and turns. I never really know how things are going to get resolved. I honestly thought things were hopeless in this one but it’s totally mindblowing to see how they always manage to pull everything off. I’ve put this series as finished but the author has said that she hasn’t put the possibility of a fourth book out and I would love to read more about this crazy team!<br /><br />I am officially in love with Kat. She’s so loyal to her family and to Hale. Their friendship and relationship is so sweet and genuine. It grew really organically and this book is kind of the culmination of that. Kat has personally grown so much from the first book. She is so much more mature and conscious of herself and what she values in life. She’s grown, she’s fierce and she’s smart. I love how she is with her family and her friends, she’ll do anything for them and it definitely showed in this book. I definitely grew to love her slowly since she has a kind of cold personality.<br /><br />Hale is one of my favorite characters from this series. He came in super charming and funny but throughout the series we get to know him deeper and more intensely. He’s a very complex character and I liked that he was more emotional in this book. He let his guard down and it showed a different side to him but he still remained his charming self. I usually talk about the rest of the side characters here, but this book in particular was more singular in its character development. So while all the side characters showed up, we didn’t really learn anything new about them. I would love to have more books about this cast though.<br /><br />Overall, this is one of my favorite series finales. The plot was fun and entertaining while keeping it’s action packed rhythm. It had a more emotional element which I enjoyed reading about and was about the group of characters coming together for one of their own. This cast of characters is really fun and unique and I hope that we get more books about them in the future. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

<div id="review_353689607" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/353689607" />
    <a title="Keertana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana"><img alt="Keertana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438801223p2/7584700.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/353689607?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Keertana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Keertana" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana">Keertana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer353689607" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2664540869214983358">Obviously, Ally Carter and I need to have a chat. A long one. Preferably ending with her releasing her books all in the summer so I don't waste my day reading instead of studying for my tests or doing my physics homework, all which I have to do now at around 10 PM. Still, I have to admit, this was worth it. <br/><br/><i>Perfect Scoundrels</i> is hands down the best HS novel so far and I hope they just continue to get better from her on out. Unlike the last two novels which focus solely on heists, <i>Perfect Scoundr</i></span>
  <span id="freeText2664540869214983358" style="display:none">Obviously, Ally Carter and I need to have a chat. A long one. Preferably ending with her releasing her books all in the summer so I don't waste my day reading instead of studying for my tests or doing my physics homework, all which I have to do now at around 10 PM. Still, I have to admit, this was worth it. <br /><br /><i>Perfect Scoundrels</i> is hands down the best HS novel so far and I hope they just continue to get better from her on out. Unlike the last two novels which focus solely on heists, <i>Perfect Scoundrels</i> is about stealing back Hale. Nope, he hasn't been kidnapped, but ever since the death of his grandmother, he hasn't been the same. Now, Kat has to do everything in her power to make it okay and bring back the Hale she knows, even if it means finding his grandmother's real will and taking on a criminal who may just be as clever as she is. <br /><br />What makes <i>Perfect Scoundrels</i> such a phenomenal novel is the mere fact that Carter has written three-dimensional characters. Finally. While her previous novels were fun, engaging, and compelling, <i>Perfect Scoundrels</i> blows them all away by exposing the more vulnerable side of Hale, showing us the deep ravine that actually separates the worlds that Hale and Kat live in, and ultimately forging stronger relationships. We get to see a different side of Hale, but also of Kat, especially since family plays a huge role in this book. Not just the family you're born into, but the family of friends you decide to trust and who remain loyal to you, no matter what. <br /><br />For me, though, <i>Perfect Scoundrels</i> came alive because of all the raw emotion in it. Carter still retains her classic style of writing, fast-paced plot lines, intelligent con plans, and she throws in a fair share of heists too, but there's so much more of everything in this novel. It is <i>more,</i> more than what we've come to expect from Carter and in the best possible way. I can now only keep my fingers crossed that this series will continue to improve and its characters will retain the depth we've been lucky enough to glimpse in this installment. <br /><br />You can read <a href="http://ivybookbindings.blogspot.com/2013/02/mini-reviews-nightmare-affair-and.html" rel="nofollow noopener">this review</a> and more on my blog, <a href="http://ivybookbindings.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Ivy Book Bindings.</a> </span>
  <a data-text-id="2664540869214983358" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_357989047" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/357989047" />
    <a title="Jasprit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4841793-jasprit"><img alt="Jasprit" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456315622p2/4841793.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/357989047?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jasprit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jasprit" href="/user/show/4841793-jasprit">Jasprit</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781408326459" href="/book/show/15848609-perfect-scoundrels">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=arc-galley">arc-galley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=out-2013">out-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer357989047" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2996697902244930283">Perfect Scoundrels in my opinion is the best from Ally Carter in the Heist Society series yet. I had my initial doubts when picking this up as Uncommon Criminals didn’t pack the punch that I’d expected; but Perfect Scoundrels was one heck of a thrilling ride and went onto show me why I fell in love with this series in the first place.<br/><br/>Kat Bishop is back, but this time the con she has to deal with is a lot closer to home, Hale’s grandma’s will is suggested to be a fake, all the evidence on the con</span>
  <span id="freeText2996697902244930283" style="display:none">Perfect Scoundrels in my opinion is the best from Ally Carter in the Heist Society series yet. I had my initial doubts when picking this up as Uncommon Criminals didn’t pack the punch that I’d expected; but Perfect Scoundrels was one heck of a thrilling ride and went onto show me why I fell in love with this series in the first place.<br /><br />Kat Bishop is back, but this time the con she has to deal with is a lot closer to home, Hale’s grandma’s will is suggested to be a fake, all the evidence on the contrary suggests so too. Kat knows it’s a con she must figure out, but doing so could hurt someone really close to her; Hale, he’s been left in charge of Hale industries, so she doesn’t want this to be true either, and the only way she can get to the bottom of this is by behind his back, something she doesn’t want to do either, so what’s a girl like Kat to do?<br /><br />It was great fun being back with the gang again, they found themselves in an unusual situation, Kat and her friends were known for being the greatest thieves, they had robbed the Henley, something which had never been done before. But now they had it all to deal with, Kat had to risk losing her friendship with Hale or Hale losing everything. As far as cons went this time, the gang definitely found themselves buried deep.<br /><br />Returning characters made Perfect Scoundrels a hoot of a read, the banter back and forth, the comradeship between Kat’s friends and family made me realise how much I missed being around them. But the series of events which occurred definitely had a damaging effect on one of my favourite characters; Hale. In the previous two books I adored Hale’s humour and his attitude to life, he was laid back, never fretted about anything and took everything in his stride. But after losing his grandma Hale was a lost and vulnerable boy, and I hated seeing this side of him. He was torn between staying true to his family, a family that had been out of the picture and his family he had made in the last two years with the Bishops. It was a tough con for everyone to deal with but especially poor Hale. The fun Heist books, we all had come to know and love, for the first time dealt with serious and heart breaking undertones.<br /><br />Despite my heart crumbling throughout most of the book, Ally Carter also had me thoroughly surprised by upping her cons. A few times I had a couple of ideas which way things would go but I was totally off the mark. The surprises kept on coming right until the very end.<br /><br />Perfect Scoundrels was an exciting follow up to Uncommon Criminals, I have secret hopes that Carter decides to continue with this wonderful series as I can’t wait to see what Kat and the rest of the gang find themselves caught up in next time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2996697902244930283" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1448236096" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1448236096" />
    <a title="rachel ☾" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17290119-rachel"><img alt="rachel ☾" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591333266p2/17290119.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1448236096?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="rachel ☾" class="user" itemprop="url" name="rachel ☾" href="/user/show/17290119-rachel">rachel ☾</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17290119-rachel?shelf=young-adult-lit">young-adult-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17290119-rachel?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1448236096" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12263750193021363896">Either I’m having problems with my memory (and let’s be real, I’m as forgetful as a hamster so that’s actually a plausible hypothesis) or the books I’ve been reading lately are just plain old forgettable. When I finished <i>Perfect Scoundrels</i> I was not unhappy with it. It was a solid read, and definitely my favourite of the series so far. But looking back I can honestly say that I barely remember it… and it’s only been a week or so since I picked it up. I’m not sure what it is that has made me dism</span>
  <span id="freeText12263750193021363896" style="display:none">Either I’m having problems with my memory (and let’s be real, I’m as forgetful as a hamster so that’s actually a plausible hypothesis) or the books I’ve been reading lately are just plain old forgettable. When I finished <i>Perfect Scoundrels</i> I was not unhappy with it. It was a solid read, and definitely my favourite of the series so far. But looking back I can honestly say that I barely remember it… and it’s only been a week or so since I picked it up. I’m not sure what it is that has made me dismiss it so easily – the ending? The character-driven plot? The lack of fast-paced action like the other two books? Whatever it is, it’s leaving me feeling rather confused. This was a solid story, <i>honestly</i>, and it made me want to see more written about Kat &amp; Hale – there’s rumours of a fourth book, but I don’t know how solid they are. <br /><br />I enjoyed how much development the characters were given in this installment. I’ve never really felt that we’ve ever truly knew the characters of the series before this book, but this entire book focused on Hale, and I just loved getting into his head a little more, learning about his life and his family, seeing his and Kat’s first meeting. It worked wonders and I thought it really bought everything built up over the last two books together nicely. The extra character development also meant that I finally supported the slow-burning-maybe-it’s-there romance between Hale and Kat.<br /><br />This also added to the story. It wasn’t just a story about stealing a jewel or a painting that belonged to someone who didn’t deserve it. This was a much more realistic and believable story. It had a personal involvement that pulled at our heartstrings and upped the cost of the outcome, making us emotionally investing in the end. I cared whether or not Kat could save the day, and I loved that this was such a high stakes con that Kat’s entire family and support network was there.<br /><br />Overall, this was definitely the best book of the series and my favourite installment. I loved the character development and the way it built up the plotline and romance. I don’t know how true the rumours of a fourth book are, but I have my finger crossed that the series can get the wrap-up it deserves. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12263750193021363896" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_404122792" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/404122792" />
    <a title="Tiff at Mostly YA Lit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4163146-tiff-at-mostly-ya-lit"><img alt="Tiff at Mostly YA Lit" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1448295560p2/4163146.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/404122792?book_show_action=true">Aug 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tiff at Mostly YA Lit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tiff at Mostly YA Lit" href="/user/show/4163146-tiff-at-mostly-ya-lit">Tiff at Mostly YA Lit</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer404122792" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7885454203851763559">4.5 out of 5 stars. <br/><br/>Guys, I read this in February, right after it came out, and it took me THIS LONG to write a review, because...Ally Carter. ALLY CARTER. I always find it incredibly hard to write reviews for her books, because they are so ridiculously well-done, and I can't critique them because there's almost nothing I would change.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380389613ra/750817.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Perfect Scoundrels is masterful plotting, crazy twists and turns, all with a really awesome premise, and characters you can't help but love. If you've read Heist S</span>
  <span id="freeText7885454203851763559" style="display:none">4.5 out of 5 stars. <br><br>Guys, I read this in February, right after it came out, and it took me THIS LONG to write a review, because...Ally Carter. ALLY CARTER. I always find it incredibly hard to write reviews for her books, because they are so ridiculously well-done, and I can't critique them because there's almost nothing I would change.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380389613ra/750817.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Perfect Scoundrels is masterful plotting, crazy twists and turns, all with a really awesome premise, and characters you can't help but love. If you've read Heist Society and Uncommon Criminals, you know what I'm talking about. Ally's books are always surprising and so amazingly well-paced that you can't help but fall into her world.<br><br>This time, the stakes are extra high, because Kat's boyfriend, Hale, has just unexpectedly inherited the family company. Hale is from a super-rich, snooty family, with jerky parents who don't care what he does with his time or anything about him. They do, however, care who owns the company.<br><br>There's a lot more Hale-Kat interaction, not just in the plotting of the heist, but also in the romantic sense. Guys, Ally Carter does NOT disappoint on this. The kisses are HOT. Like, STEAMY. I can't say anything more than that. Here's a gif. =p<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380389613ra/750818.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="http://mostlyyalit.blogspot.ca/2013/04/review-perfect-scoundrels-by-ally-carter.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Read the rest of this review at Mostly YA Lit</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7885454203851763559" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2766672-dark-faerie-tales?shelf=reviewed-by-kayla">reviewed-by-kayla</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer587531450" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15307814445949940365">Review courtesy of Dark Faerie Tales.<br/><br/>Quick & Dirty: Carter weaves yet another thrilling mystery with more than a few twists to keep you on your toes and begging for more. Plus there’s more insight on the history of the amazingly gorgeous (and rich) W.W. Hale.<br/><br/>Opening Sentence: Of all the people who knew about the big house in the middle of Wyndham Woods, very few had ever been inside.<br/><br/>The Review: <br/><br/>Kat and Hale’s relationship has been drifting past the border of friendship for some time, but in this</span>
  <span id="freeText15307814445949940365" style="display:none">Review courtesy of Dark Faerie Tales.<br /><br />Quick &amp; Dirty: Carter weaves yet another thrilling mystery with more than a few twists to keep you on your toes and begging for more. Plus there’s more insight on the history of the amazingly gorgeous (and rich) W.W. Hale.<br /><br />Opening Sentence: Of all the people who knew about the big house in the middle of Wyndham Woods, very few had ever been inside.<br /><br />The Review: <br /><br />Kat and Hale’s relationship has been drifting past the border of friendship for some time, but in this book it seems that they are secretly dating–well, secretly to Hale’s family. But it’s when Hale unexpectedly leaves on a heist that their relationship goes from sweet and warm to an icy shoulder. Then Kat sees the headline on the next day’s newspaper: the Hazel Hale, CEO of Hale Industries and Hale’s beloved grandmother, died that night, about the same time Hale left her stranded in a window. Now the entire Hale family has convened for the funeral – and most importantly – the reading of the will. But Hale’s mostly silent but always reliable butler hires Kat and her crew for the most unlikely of cons. He thinks that the will has been forged and now Hale, who just inherited the entirety of Hale Industries, is the mark. As Hale grows more distant, Kat has to decide if her usual partner in crime is able to follow through with the plan – and the possibilities that come with its success. Ally Carter spins another wonderfully intricate and clever tale that is sure to keep you guessing.<br /><br />This by far is the best Heist Society book yet. The plot, as always, never goes the way you think, and the multiple missions throughout are cleverly developed. I’m always a fan of Carter’s writing, but I think that the highlight of the book were the characters. We’re given more insight into Hale’s family and the environment he grew up with. AND Hale and Kat’s first meeting is described perfectly (see Notable Scene), introducing Hale and Kat’s relationship and the catalyst of the story – Hale’s grandmother.<br /><br />Despite Kat’s face on the cover, the spotlight character of this book is the handsome fellow in the reflection of the sunglasses. W.W. Hale’s history has always been an enigma, but in this book its splayed out for everyone to see. Beside’s Hale’s loyal and rich exterior, we finally get to view his vulnerable side – the side that’s affected by the constant disappointment from his parents and the competition between family members. I loved that Carter delved deep into his character development and wasn’t afraid to turn our self-controlled rich boy into a grief-stricken teenager that just lost the only family member that saw the potential in him. And I pity Kat for having to put up with him.<br /><br />I appreciate Kat in this book. Although she struggles with her want to keep Hale close to her, she’s always trying to do what’s best for him, even when he’s constantly pushing her away. This book not only tests Hale, but it also tests Kat as she deals with the responsibility of the con and the constant waiting for Hale to finally come to terms with the hand he has been dealt. My heart broke for her a few times throughout the book (my heart heals fast) and when I would have given up, she kept pressing on, trying the impossible – and pulling everyone in with her.<br /><br />Overall, I loved this book. There was more of Uncle Eddie (who is my favorite minor character because of his infamy in heists), the return of several old characters and, of course, the freaking heart-stopping-I-can’t-believe-that-happened ending that I refuse to spoil. No cliffhangers, but I can definitely see potential for new books in the future. Hopefully Carter will be able to continue the series, but in the meantime, read this book (or the entire series) if you know what’s good for you! <br /><br />Notable Scene: <br /><br />“You’re not supposed to be here,” the girl said.<br /><br />“Funny, I was going to say the same thing to you.” He smiled like his night had just gotten significantly more interesting.<br /><br />“You don’t seem afraid,” the girl said.<br /><br />“Well, that makes two of us.”<br /><br />Spotlights shone down, and the boy studied her in the manner of someone who is used to looking at rare, beautiful things. Then he jerked his head at the painting and said, “Okay. Go ahead, take it.”<br /><br />He started to leave, but stopped when the girl said, “Yeah, I can have this one. It’s a fake.”<br /><br />“Oh now, that hurts.” He brought a hand to his chest like he’d been stabbed. “Not that it’s any of your business, but the Hale family happens to have the largest collection of Monets in the United States.”<br /><br />“Technically, it’s the largest private collection. And this isn’t one of them. This”–she shined a small flashlight onto the delicate brushstrokes–”is a slightly better-than-average forgery.”<br /><br />When the boy eased closer to the painting, it was like he was seeing it for the first time. “No. That can’t be right.”<br /><br />“Sorry to break it to you.”<br /><br />He shook his head slowly. “But my grandmother said…”<br /><br />“She lied.”<br /><br />The boy smiled again and whispered something that sounded like “Hazel is awesome,” but the girl wasn’t quite sure.<br /><br />FTC Advisory: Hyperion Books for Children provided me with a copy of Perfect Scoundrels. No goody bags, sponsorships, “material connections,” or bribes were exchanged for my review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15307814445949940365" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

Of course I'm going to read a book about thieves.<br/><br/><i>Awesome Author</i><br/><br/><img height='131' src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380388811ra/749622.gif' width='200' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I love Ally Carter's YA books.   <span id="freeText18259636363533963445" style="display:none">More shenanigans to be had over at <a href="http://ransom-reads.blogspot.com.au" rel="nofollow noopener">Ransom Reads</a><br><br>MAJOR SELLING POINTS:<br><br><i>Thieves!</i><br><br><img height="101" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380388811ra/749621.gif" width="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Do I really need to explain why thieves is one of the main selling points? Thieves are awesome. They're in league with spies, assassins, and pirates. Of course I'm going to read a book about thieves.<br><br><i>Awesome Author</i><br><br><img height="131" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380388811ra/749622.gif" width="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I love Ally Carter's YA books. They're always funny with nice fast plot lines. Very enjoyable reads about interesting people (spies and thieves. I will never get enough). Chances are I'm going to buy any YA she publishes.<br><br><b>SWASHBUCKLING:</b><br><br><img height="111" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380388811ra/749623.gif" width="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm sick so my thoughts aren't flowing too well, but I must try and explain my thoughts on the plot. IT WAS SO GOOD. We got to see old characters and meet a few who had only been mentioned/we knew existed but never seen, as well as return to some locations from previous Heist books. In terms of the con, nothing was what I thought it was. When I was convinced a particular event would happen, there would be a twist to prove me wrong. Then there would be a twist about that twist. And then... GAH! Magnificent. I never predicted it. <br><br><b>LINGO:</b><br><br><img height="128" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380388811ra/749624.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This was written in the manner I expected from Ally Carter. Humourous with touching moments. Some of the descriptions of heists and cons were the best. I loved the interactions between characters, the dialogue sequences were particular highlights.<br><br><b>CREW:</b><br><br><i>Katarina Bishop</i><br><br><img height="124" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380388811ra/749625.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Kat is the idea girl always willing to try what every other member of her 'family' thinks is insane and impossible and nine times out of ten pulls it off. She's great. Funny, caring, smart, and dedicated, I really love her. I hope we get to see her face more challenges in this series.<br><br><i>W.W. Hale V</i><br><br><img height="131" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380388811ra/749626.gif" width="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Hale is as strangely attractive as ever. And in this book he causes us a lot of feels. We finally get to learn more about his family and see his 'other life'. It's... not nice, poor boy. The events of this novel had a big effect on him and he reacted in ways I never thought he would. It was good to see he's a normal teenager sometimes.<br><br><i>Marcus</i><br><br><img height="200" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380388811ra/749627.gif" width="163" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>In PERFECT SCOUNDRELS we see and hear more or Marcus than we ever have before. Previously, he was just Hale's loyal servant. Now, he remains in the same role, but we see his loyalty extends beyond his job. I love him so much more.<br><br><b>SWOONABILITY:</b><br><br><img height="101" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380388812ra/749628.gif" width="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>KAT AND HALE ARE TOGETHER. IT"S ABOUT BLOODY TIME!! <br><br>*ahem*<br>I'm not sure what else to write other than I'm so happy! My OTP are together! They did have a lot of troubles in this book however, and it was so sweet to see their relationship develop and evolve. Do not fear though, the romance is only a side part of the novel and really doesn't interfere with the plot that much. Maybe all it does is give Kat a few motivations she never had before.<br><br><b>SHIPS:</b><br>Hale x Kat<br>Hale x SCOOTER (I still can't believe SCOOTER. LOL)<br>The family x cons<br>Uncle Eddie x Life<br>Us x The meaning of Hale's initials (which still haven't been revealed *shakes fist*) </span>

<div id="review_438785923" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/438785923" />
    <a title="Mundie Moms &amp; Mundie Kids" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4397975-mundie-moms-mundie-kids"><img alt="Mundie Moms &amp; Mundie Kids" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1319228268p2/4397975.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/438785923?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mundie Moms &amp; Mundie Kids" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mundie Moms &amp; Mundie Kids" href="/user/show/4397975-mundie-moms-mundie-kids">Mundie Moms &amp; Mundie Kids</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4397975-mundie-moms-mundie-kids?shelf=2013-reading-challenge">2013-reading-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4397975-mundie-moms-mundie-kids?shelf=mundie-moms-reviews">mundie-moms-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4397975-mundie-moms-mundie-kids?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4397975-mundie-moms-mundie-kids?shelf=2013-release">2013-release</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer438785923" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1978494025474812444">My review, the shortened version: <br/><br/>I LOVED THIS BOOK! GO PICK IT UP!<br/><br/>My review, the full version: <br/><br/>I seriously love this series and loved what Ally did with Kat and Hale's storyline. I don't know what else to add to what I mentioned in my shortened review. I mean, I have plenty to say, but I can't talk in detail about the awesomeness of Kat & Hale, and Ally's writing without given sounding like a rambling fangirl. There is something about Ally's writing that I fall victim to every time I sit down t</span>
  <span id="freeText1978494025474812444" style="display:none">My review, the shortened version: <br /><br />I LOVED THIS BOOK! GO PICK IT UP!<br /><br />My review, the full version: <br /><br />I seriously love this series and loved what Ally did with Kat and Hale's storyline. I don't know what else to add to what I mentioned in my shortened review. I mean, I have plenty to say, but I can't talk in detail about the awesomeness of Kat &amp; Hale, and Ally's writing without given sounding like a rambling fangirl. There is something about Ally's writing that I fall victim to every time I sit down to read one of her books. My intended goal of reading for a few minutes turns into many more and minutes then a hour, then two, and then I'm finished with the book. I can't help myself. I'm addicted to Kat &amp; Hale's story, and Ally's writing. This story, like the other two books in the series is fabulous! It's one of my all time favorite series. <br /><br />Okay let's be honest, we all adore Kat, but we all love Hale. This is the first time in the series where I've felt like Ally really allowed me to see the vulnerable side of Hale. I admit, it left me a little heartbroken, and like Kat, really worried about the direction this broken boy was going to take. In true Hale fashion, he also completely surprised me. Oh Hale. Boy does he ever make me want to slap him, and hug him all at the same time. I think I was about as shocked as Kat was over a few of his scenes and how he acts and treats her. Though it it understandable that there is something going on and I loved Kat for being the strong one and not giving up on him. <br /><br />Kat. I didn't think I could love her anymore than I already did, but Ally made her this incredibly strong, stubborn character who was on a mission to figure out what was really going on with Hale. I swear Kat is one con artist you can't out con, and this time around her entire family is behind her, helping her uncover what's going on at Hale Industries. Aside from loving Kat and Hale, I adore Kat's family! Each of the characters who make up her family add just the right touch of family dynamics, humor and smarts that even though they're con artists, they have this great family relationship I enjoy getting glimpses off, whether it be in Uncle Eddie's kitchen, on the job, or some place else. <br /><br />Oh the romance! It's one those romances that makes you yearn for those stolen glances and secret moments that Kat and Hale have together. It's sweet, fragile, complex, and a little something more. I should have known based on how Perfect Scoundrels started, giving readers a glimpse into the first time Hale and Kat meet, how this storyline was going to go. Hale and Kat had me from that moment at the window, on. I enjoyed how that first meeting and their relationship play a crucial role with this story. One of my favorite jokes with Kat's family involves a wager of goats. You'll know why I love it when you read it. ;) Yes it has something to do with their relationship and no cheating and reading the last page of the book, because you won't get the joke until you read the scene the joke starts in.<br /><br />Perfect Scoundrels is a that perfect read when you're wanting to sit down with a good book, who's storyline takes you out of the real world for a bit. It gives you real characters you wish you could crawl into the book and hang out with, exciting world travels rip with danger, and a sweet romance that leaves you anticipating what will happen next with Kat and Hale. Above all you'll get an an entertaining storyline you won't be able to get enough of. I HIGHLY recommend picking this book up today!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1978494025474812444" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('KkchcLYVRULjkMzkrsmCkAwxCzyzt3Qs9wJsZ03CumYyVXdrt9X4cF7TDrfGNBPC0meixURu+GrijtOyemc7fA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('fK0L64lZL6oMxHT+IS9nNBRAaALXKTDIVJaMY7iFsstkv13wiJmSmLGHtq1J0vZmyhbB+yDwvI5BGjO2jyAz0Q==')})
  }
